Welcome to ARIA V4 Connector

By updating to V4, ARIA becomes the only ML (machine learning) EA through XGBoost that performs cross-control with external AIs, since all XGBoost predictions are double-checked with ARIA's AI engines to validate signals before execution.

XGBoost is one of the most awarded and competitive algorithms in the world of predictive analytics, which has been trained with 60,000 real audited trades collected through the ARIA Audit API + Render.

This cross-verification ensures safer entries and exits, combining the mathematical strength of XGBoost with the contextual intelligence of AI models.

This version brings numerous changes and improvements. It is much more intuitive for new users and better organized for those who were already using previous versions.

We will start with a step-by-step guide to install ARIA from scratch. If you already know the procedure, you can skip to the next section.

Important: This guide contains complete step-by-step instructions for ARIA V4. Follow each section carefully to ensure optimal performance.

ğŸ¯ What is ARIA XGBoost?

ğŸ“– Simple Definition

ARIA XGBoost is an artificial intelligence system integrated into your EA that automatically predicts the best Stop Loss (SL) and Take Profit (TP) levels for each trade, based on analysis of more than 60,000 real historical trades.

ğŸš€ Why is it revolutionary?

  • ğŸ§  Real intelligence: Doesn't use fixed formulas, but patterns learned from real trades
  • ğŸ“Š Massive database: 890 audit reports with 60,000+ analyzed trades
  • ğŸ¯ Personalized predictions: Each SL/TP calculated specifically for current market conditions
  • ğŸ“ˆ Continuous improvement: System learns from new data constantly

ğŸ”„ How Does It Work?

âš™ï¸ Automatic Process in 3 Steps

ğŸ“Š STEP 1: Current Market Analysis

When EA detects a trade opportunity, it automatically collects:

  • Technical indicators: RSI, ATR, Moving Averages, Spread
  • Market conditions: Volatility, time of day, day of week
  • Trade data: Symbol, direction (BUY/SELL), entry price
ğŸ” STEP 2: Intelligent Search

XGBoost system searches the database of 60,000+ trades to find:

  • Similar trades with same market conditions
  • Successful patterns that worked in similar situations
  • Common errors that caused losses in the past
ğŸ¯ STEP 3: Optimized Prediction

Based on historical analysis, it calculates:

  • Optimal Stop Loss: Protection based on real data
  • Realistic Take Profit: Achievable target according to history
  • Confidence level: Success probability (50-95%)
  • Trade quality: High/Medium/Low evaluation

â“ Frequently Asked Questions

ğŸ”§ Technical Questions

Q: Do I need to install anything additional?

A: No. Everything works automatically once the EA is compiled. You only need the .ex5 file.

Q: Does it work without internet connection?

A: Not for XGBoost, but automatic fallback guarantees EA continues working with traditional methods.

Q: Can I use XGBoost only for SL or only for TP?

A: Yes. You can configure SL Mode: XGBoost ML and TP Mode: Fixed Pips or any combination.

Q: What happens if confidence is very low?

A: If confidence is below configured minimum (e.g., 65%), system automatically uses fallback method.

Q: Is my trading data sent to any server?

A: Only technical market data (RSI, ATR, etc.) is sent to get predictions. No personal or account information is sent.

Q: Can I see what data is being sent?

A: Yes. Activate Debug Mode: TRUE to see detailed logs of all communications.

Q: Does the system improve over time?

A: Yes. Each new trade adds data to the system, continuously improving predictions.

Q: What happens if Render is down?

A: System automatically detects failure and uses fallback method. Your trading is never interrupted.

Problem: Confidence always <65%
Solution:

  • âœ… Verify market conditions
  • âœ… May be normal in uncertain markets
3. XGBoost doesn't activate
Problem: Always uses fallback
Solution:
  • âœ… Verify Use XGBoost: TRUE
  • âœ… Verify SL/TP Mode: XGBoost ML
  • âœ… Verify connectivity to Render

Installation

Installation from Zero

Complete installation process for ARIA V4 Connector.

If you had a previous version installed (e.g., V3), follow these steps:

  1. Remove ARIA from your MT5 terminal.
  2. Close all open pairs.
  3. Close the terminal completely.
  4. Reopen it and make sure ARIA no longer appears in Experts.
  5. Connect to MQL5 and download the new ARIA V4 version.
Important: Complete removal of previous versions ensures no conflicts with the new V4 installation.
Step 1

Enable AutoTrading and WebRequest

Before placing the EA on a chart, it's essential to configure the following settings.

MT5 Configuration:

  1. In MT5, go to Tools â†’ Options â†’ Expert Advisors.
  2. Check these boxes:
    • âœ… Allow algorithmic trading
    • âœ… Allow WebRequest for listed URL

Add these URLs:

ğŸ¤– Primary AI Provider

  • https://openrouter.ai/ â†’ With this AI provider you only need to manage a single API Key
  • https://nfs.faireconomy.media/ â†’ From here we will obtain important news
  • https://aria-mcp-bridge.onrender.com â†’ XGBoost server for advanced analysis
  • https://aria-audit-api.onrender.com â†’ Render audit API for trade analysis

ğŸ”— Direct Provider URLs (Optional)

If you want to connect directly to each provider separately, you should also add these URLs:

  • https://api.x.ai/
  • https://api.mistral.ai/
  • https://api.deepseek.com
  • https://api.anthropic.com/
  • https://generativelanguage.googleapis.com
  • https://api.together.xyz/
  • https://api.openai.com
ğŸ“Œ Your configuration should look like this:
Step 2

AutoTrading Configuration on Chart

Configure AutoTrading settings when placing ARIA on your chart.

  1. Open any trading pair and place ARIA on the chart.
  2. Verify the following:
    • The AutoTrading button in the toolbar must be green/active.
    • In EA Properties â†’ Common tab, enable:
      • âœ… Allow live trading

This confirms that AutoTrading is enabled in all necessary places and that ARIA has permissions to connect to:

  • ğŸ“° Economic news
  • ğŸ¤– AI providers
  • ğŸ§  XGBoost server
OpenRouter

Get OpenRouter API Key

How to get OpenRouter ApiKey

Remember: You can obtain a single key from OpenRouter and access the 112 available AIs (here are the free AIs), or configure a direct connection with specific providers (ideal for using paid AIs).
ğŸŒ Geographic Availability: OpenRouter is available in all countries, unlike some direct AIs like OpenAI or Gemini that, for example, are not available in China. We suggest using OpenRouter when your geographic area is affected by local restrictions.

1. Create an Account

  1. Go to ğŸ‘‰ https://openrouter.ai
  2. Click Sign Up (or "Continue with Google" if you prefer).
  3. Verify your email address.
  4. Log in to your OpenRouter dashboard.

2. Make the $10 Deposit (One-Time Unlock)

To unlock the 1,000 free AIs queries per day, OpenRouter requires a one-time deposit of $10.

Without this deposit, your account will be limited to only 10â€“20 free queries per day.

The deposit is not consumed by the free AIs. It simply activates the higher daily limit for 1 year.

Your wallet will still show the $10 balance untouched, as long as you only use the free models.

Now, here's how to make the deposit:

  1. In the top menu, go to Billing â†’ Wallet.
  2. Click Deposit Funds.
  3. Enter $10 (the minimum required).
  4. Choose your payment method:
    • Credit/Debit Card
    • PayPal
    • Sometimes Crypto (availability depends on region)
  5. Confirm the payment.

Once completed, your wallet will display a balance (e.g., $10.00) and your account will be upgraded to the higher limit.

3. Generate Your API Key

In your dashboard, go to API Keys:

  1. Click Create New Key.
  2. Give it a name, e.g., ARIA
  3. Copy the key immediately and save it (you'll need it in ARIA).
  4. Example format: sk-or-xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx

4. Go to MT5 and insert Your API Key into ARIA

For user convenience, ARIA API keys are loaded from a "keys.txt" file located in the MQL5/Files folder. This is done only once, then you won't need to load it for each pair. In this file, you load all the API keys you want to use: OpenRouter and other providers.

Important: Never share your API key with anyone.

5. Which AIs to use?

By default, we recommend using the free AIs. You can enable just one, or multiple ones to perform voting, depending on your personal preference (or the preset you selected).

For those who requested it, we've also included the option to use paid AIs:

  • If you want to use paid AIs, you'll need to deposit at least $20 instead of $10.
  • In this case, tokens will be deducted for each query. The cost is very small and becomes negligible when compared to the profits of each trade, so there's no need to worry about expenses.

By default, Free AIs = True. If you wish to use the paid AIs, set Free AIs = False and Paid AIs = True.

The same API key works for both free and paid AIs.

Keys

ğŸ”‘ Place your API Key

Simplified API Key management in ARIA V4.

ğŸ¯ New in V4: Starting from V4, you will only need to place the API Key(s) once. These APIs will be stored in a file hosted within MQL5/files, under the name "Keys.txt".

ğŸ“‚ How the Keys.txt File Works

ğŸ”„ Automatic File Generation

When you place ARIA on a chart for the first time, this file will be generated automatically.

ğŸ“ File Location: MQL5/Files/Keys.txt

âš™ï¸ One-Time Configuration

For the first and only time, you will need to place the corresponding API Key in the list for each AI provider you want to use.

âš ï¸ Important Format: Pay special attention to the format, for example:
  • OpenRouter=(without leaving a space) api key
  • Mistral=(without leaving a space) api key
  • Grok=(without leaving a space) api key

ğŸ’¾ Save and Forget

Once you save all the API keys for all the providers you want to use, save the file.

ğŸ‰ Done! You no longer need to worry about loading an API Key. From now on, you will only need to select the AI provider(s) you want to use from the configuration panel.
ğŸ“‹ Workflow Summary:
  1. First time: Place ARIA on chart â†’ Keys.txt auto-generated
  2. Configure once: Edit Keys.txt with your API keys
  3. Save file: Save Keys.txt with all your providers
  4. Select providers: Use configuration panel to choose AIs
  5. Trade: No more API key management needed!
AIs

AIs and Tokens

Understanding AI usage, token consumption, and optimization strategies.

ğŸ¤– Is it necessary to use all 7 AIs?

No, it's not required. ARIA can operate correctly with just one provider.

The number of supported AIs has been expanded to 7 to give users the flexibility to choose their preferred providers from a broad range of available options.

However, it's better to always use multiple AIs (e.g., 2, 3, or 4) since these activate a voting system and there will be greater diversity of opinions.

ğŸ”¢ How many AIs are recommended?

ğŸ’° Paid Models

3 AIs are sufficient if they are paid models.

  • Higher accuracy and reliability
  • Consistent response times
  • Better signal quality

ğŸ†“ Free Models

4 AIs are recommended because free AIs sometimes may not respond or give errors, and in this case we will always have at least one extra.

  • Backup redundancy
  • Error tolerance
  • Maintained voting system

ğŸš€ Advanced Configurations

We also have some presets that have worked very well with 5-7 AIs, so this remains each trader's decision.

  • Maximum diversity of opinions
  • Robust voting system
  • Higher accuracy potential

ğŸ’¸ How much do AIs consume?

It depends on what you have activated, depending on the number of queries you make per day and the data you send.

High Consumption Scenarios:

If you use the fractal filter on multiple timeframes and also send data from the last 100 candles, your consumption will skyrocket since the data sent to the AIs plus what the AIs have to process is much higher.

It is suggested to see how many tokens your strategy consumes.

Token Optimization Tips:
  • Monitor usage: Check token consumption regularly
  • Optimize filters: Use fractal filters selectively
  • Adjust data sent: Reduce candle history if consumption is high
  • Choose providers wisely: Balance cost vs performance

âœï¸ V4 Prompt Optimization

Although when multiple consultation is performed, the default prompt is optimized, now in V4, the prompt will be editable, so depending on what you send, you can consume more or fewer tokens.

New Feature: Editable prompts in V4 allow for custom optimization based on your specific trading strategy and token budget.
Temperature

AI Temperature

The AI Temperature parameter in ARIA Connector EA controls the creativity and variability of responses from the artificial intelligence models that the EA consults.

ğŸ“Œ How it Works

Temperature is a value between 0.0 and 1.0 (in some providers up to 2.0).

ğŸ§Š Low Temperature (e.g. 0.0 â€“ 0.3)

  • More deterministic and repeatable responses
  • AI will tend to always give the same conclusion when faced with similar data
  • Ideal for trading because it reduces randomness and improves consistency
Best for: Single AI configurations where consistency is paramount.

ğŸŒ¡ï¸ Medium Temperature (e.g. 0.4 â€“ 0.7)

Default: Use this medium range

  • Generates a certain degree of variation in predictions
  • Can detect alternative opportunities, but with more dispersion in results
  • Balanced approach between consistency and flexibility
Best for: Multiple AI voting systems where some variation helps capture different perspectives.

ğŸ”¥ High Temperature (e.g. 0.8 â€“ 1.0+)

  • Much more creative and less predictable responses
  • Can be useful in research or testing, but in trading increases the risk of incoherent signals
  • Not recommended for live trading
âš ï¸ Risk: High temperature can produce contradictory recommendations between different AI providers.

ğŸ¯ Temperature Recommendations

General Guidelines:

It's generally advisable to keep the temperature low or medium-low to prioritize stability over creativity.

âš ï¸ High Temperature Risks

A temperature that is too high can produce contradictory recommendations between different AI providers.

ğŸ”’ Low Temperature Risks

If the temperature is too low, it can generate certain rigidity. If multiple AIs have to vote, good trading opportunities that would have been profitable might be missed.

ğŸ¤– Single AI Configuration

If you are using 1 single AI, you can afford lower temperature for maximum consistency.

Single AI Advantage: With only one AI, lower temperature ensures highly consistent signals without the need for voting diversity.

ğŸ“Š Temperature Impact Summary

Key Takeaways:
  • ğŸ¯ Recommended Range: 0.4 - 0.7 for most configurations
  • ğŸ¤– Single AI: Can use lower temperature (0.0 - 0.3)
  • ğŸ—³ï¸ Multiple AI: Medium temperature (0.4 - 0.7) for voting diversity
  • âš ï¸ Avoid High: Temperature above 0.8 increases signal inconsistency
Prompts

Editable Prompts

ARIA V4 Connector incorporates one of the most requested features: the ability to edit prompts directly without needing to modify the EA code.

âš ï¸ For Experienced Users Only: This is an option only for experienced users. If you are a new user, please leave this option as false and do not edit the prompts to avoid errors.

ğŸ”‘ Key Functions with Editable Prompts

ğŸ“‚ Management from TXT Files

Prompts are located in the folder:

MQL5/FILES/PROMPTS

You can edit them from there and load them directly from the ARIA Configuration Panel, in the PROMPTS tab.

ğŸ¨ Total Customization

You can modify the prompts that ARIA sends to the AIs according to your strategy or trading style.

âš ï¸ Important: You must respect the parameters enclosed in braces { } (example: {timeframe}), as they are internal variables that should not be deleted or altered.

ğŸ“‹ Reusable Templates

Save different prompt formats, for example:

  • "Scalping Mode"
  • "Swing Mode"

Activate them according to the pair, timeframe, or preset you are using.

ğŸ›ï¸ Detail Level Control

Freely adjust aspects such as:

  • The level of depth in responses
  • The output language
  • The format: quick summaries or detailed analysis

ğŸ§© Hybrid Strategies

With this flexibility, you can create custom combinations, for example:

ğŸ“Š Technical Analysis Priority

A prompt that prioritizes technical analysis.

Use Case: Focus AI on chart patterns, indicators, and technical signals.

âš¡ Scalping Style Priority

A prompt that prioritizes a trading style, for example Scalping.

Use Case: Optimize AI responses for quick trades and rapid decision-making.

ğŸ”„ Pattern Detection

A prompt that sends the AI the last 50 candles to detect reversal or continuation patterns (with this prompt you must have candle sending activated in the parameters).

Use Case: Deep pattern analysis for swing trading and trend identification.

ğŸ› ï¸ Prompt Editing Workflow

  1. Access prompts: Go to MQL5/FILES/PROMPTS or use Configuration Panel â†’ PROMPTS tab
  2. Edit content: Modify prompt text while preserving {variables}
  3. Save template: Give descriptive names (e.g., "Scalping_Mode", "Pattern_Detection")
  4. Test prompt: Try with single AI first to verify functionality
  5. Apply to strategy: Activate in your trading configuration
  6. Monitor results: Check AI responses and token consumption

Timezone

ğŸŒ Timezone Converter

Understanding how to convert preset timezones according to your broker's geographic location.

ğŸš¨ Critical Information: Presets ALWAYS use broker server time, NOT your local time or VPS time.

â“ Why Timezone Conversion Matters

ğŸŒ The Timezone Challenge

ARIA V4 users presets are configured with specific trading hours that work optimally for certain market sessions. However, these hours are set according to the broker's server timezone, which varies by broker and geographic location.

ğŸ“Š Example Problem:
  • Preset says: Trade from 08:00 to 17:00
  • Your expectation: European session (08:00-17:00 GMT)
  • Reality: Depends on your broker's server timezone!

ğŸ• Common Broker Timezones

ğŸŒ Most Common Server Times

ğŸ‡ªğŸ‡º GMT+2/GMT+3 (European Brokers)
  • Winter: GMT+2 (EET)
  • Summer: GMT+3 (EEST)
  • Examples: Many EU-regulated brokers
ğŸ‡ºğŸ‡¸ GMT-5/GMT-4 (US Brokers)
  • Winter: GMT-5 (EST)
  • Summer: GMT-4 (EDT)
  • Examples: US-based brokers
ğŸ‡¦ğŸ‡º GMT+10/GMT+11 (Australian Brokers)
  • Winter: GMT+10 (AEST)
  • Summer: GMT+11 (AEDT)
  • Examples: Australian brokers
ğŸŒ GMT+0 (London Time)
  • Winter: GMT+0 (GMT)
  • Summer: GMT+1 (BST)
  • Examples: UK-based brokers
ğŸ‡§ğŸ‡· GMT-3 (South American Brokers)
  • Year-round: GMT-3 (BRT - Brazil Time)
  • Note: Some regions may observe daylight saving
  • Examples: Brazilian and some Latin American brokers

ğŸ”„ How to Convert Preset Times

ğŸ“ Step-by-Step Conversion Process

  1. ğŸ” Identify Your Broker's Timezone
    • Contact broker support directly to ask for their server GMT offset
    • This is the most reliable way to get accurate timezone information
  2. ğŸ“Š Determine Preset's Original Timezone
    • Most presets are created for GMT+2/GMT+3
    • Check preset documentation if available
    • Ask directly to the person who uploaded the preset about their GMT configuration (usually users mention what GMT their broker uses so you can calculate it correctly)
  3. âš™ï¸ Calculate Time Difference
    • Find difference between preset timezone and your broker
    • Apply adjustment to all trading hours
    • Consider daylight saving changes

ğŸ“Š Conversion Examples

ğŸŒ Real-World Conversion Scenarios

ğŸ“ˆ Scenario 1: European Preset â†’ US Broker
  • Preset timezone: GMT+3 (European summer)
  • Your broker: GMT-4 (US summer)
  • Time difference: 7 hours behind
  • Preset time: 08:00-17:00
  • Your broker time: 01:00-10:00
ğŸ“ˆ Scenario 2: European Preset â†’ Australian Broker
  • Preset timezone: GMT+2 (European winter)
  • Your broker: GMT+10 (Australian winter)
  • Time difference: 8 hours ahead
  • Preset time: 08:00-17:00
  • Your broker time: 16:00-01:00 (next day)
ğŸ“ˆ Scenario 3: US Preset â†’ European Broker
  • Preset timezone: GMT-5 (US winter)
  • Your broker: GMT+2 (European winter)
  • Time difference: 7 hours ahead
  • Preset time: 09:00-18:00
  • Your broker time: 16:00-01:00 (next day)
ğŸ“ˆ Scenario 4: European Preset â†’ South American Broker
  • Preset timezone: GMT+2 (European winter)
  • Your broker: GMT-3 (Brazilian broker)
  • Time difference: 5 hours behind
  • Preset time: 08:00-17:00
  • Your broker time: 03:00-12:00

âš ï¸ Important Considerations

ğŸš¨ Critical Points to Remember

ğŸ• Daylight Saving Time (DST):
  • GMT offsets change twice per year
  • European DST: Last Sunday in March/October
  • US DST: Second Sunday in March, First Sunday in November
  • Update your conversions when DST changes occur
ğŸŒ Server Time vs Local Time:
  • Always use broker server time, never your local time
  • VPS time is irrelevant for trading hours
  • Check MT5 terminal for actual server time
ğŸ“… Weekend and Holiday Considerations:
  • Market sessions may be affected by holidays
  • Some brokers have different weekend hours
  • Crypto markets operate 24/7

ğŸ”§ Practical Implementation

âœ… How to Apply Timezone Conversion

  1. ğŸ“¥ Download Preset
    • Get the preset file from community
    • Note the original timezone if mentioned
  2. ğŸ” Check Your Broker Time
    • Contact your broker support to get their GMT offset
    • This ensures accurate timezone information
  3. âš™ï¸ Adjust Trading Hours
    • Apply timezone difference to all time parameters
    • Update Start Hour, End Hour for each day
    • Adjust news filter times if applicable
  4. ğŸ’¾ Save Modified Preset
    • Save with new name indicating your timezone
    • Example: "EURUSD_Scalping_GMT-4.set"
  5. ğŸ§ª Test and Verify
    • Test on demo account first
    • Verify trading hours match expected market sessions
    • Monitor for a few days to confirm timing
ğŸ’¡ Pro Tip: Create a personal timezone conversion chart for quick reference when downloading new presets. Keep track of your broker's GMT offset for both summer and winter periods.
ğŸ“Š Final Reminder: Remember that successful trading depends not just on the right strategy, but also on trading at the right times. Proper timezone conversion ensures your EA operates during the intended market sessions for optimal performance.

New Configuration Panel

This is a completely renovated and interactive panel.

ğŸ¯ Panel Overview

From this panel, you can access all ARIA configuration without needing to edit the input parameters. This has been designed to facilitate users' configuration of ARIA, without having to look at a long list of parameters that confuse.

This panel is organized in different tabs, in a more intuitive way and with a more dynamic interface.

Panel Advantages:
  • ğŸ¨ Intuitive Interface: No more confusing parameter lists
  • ğŸ“‘ Organized Tabs: Logical grouping of settings
  • ğŸ”„ Dynamic Interface: Interactive and user-friendly
  • âš¡ Quick Configuration: Easy navigation between settings

ğŸ”§ How the Panel Works

ğŸ“‹ Scenario 1: Creating New Configuration

If you don't have a specific preset, but want to start operating and choose your options within the parameters:

  1. Navigate through tabs: Simply change all the parameters you want from the panel, just navigate comfortably tab by tab and configure what you need.
  2. Save your configuration: Once configured, you can save it, give it a specific name like a normal preset, just as you would in the parameters but in a more intuitive way.
  3. Preset storage: This preset will be saved in MQL5/Files
  4. Load in ARIA: Simply open ARIA configuration, go to the Inputs tab and load that preset you configured as you normally do.
  5. Apply settings: Load / search for the preset in MQL5/Files and that's it, when you click accept, ARIA will start operating with that preset.
âš ï¸ Important: This last step is always necessary, because MQL5 has a restriction so that no panel can directly modify the inputs configuration tab for security reasons.

ğŸ“¥ Scenario 2: Using Existing Preset

If you already have a preset that was shared by another user:

  1. Load existing preset: Simply go to the Inputs tab, click Load and search for your preset and accept.
  2. Panel auto-update: Once you click accept, the panel will be updated with the data loaded from your preset.
  3. Modify if desired: From there you can modify if you want, and save the preset from the panel itself.
  4. Apply changes: Remember that for the change to be applied in the inputs tab, you must reload the modified preset in Load / load the preset and click accept.
  5. Ready to trade: Now you have a modified preset working correctly.
Workflow Summary:
  • New Configuration: Panel â†’ Save â†’ Load in Inputs â†’ Accept
  • Existing Preset: Load in Inputs â†’ Panel Updates â†’ Modify â†’ Save â†’ Reload â†’ Accept
ğŸ”„ Key Concept: The panel and inputs tab work together. The panel provides an easy interface, but changes must always be applied through the inputs tab due to MQL5 security restrictions.

Parameters

Parameters Guide

Complete parameters configuration for ARIA V4.

Single AI Consultation

Select AI Provider

This parameter is used when working with a single AI.

From the dropdown menu you choose which provider you are going to use (OpenAI, Mistral, DeepSeek, Claude, etc.).

AI Configuration

Each provider has its own section (example: Llama, Gemini, Claude, DeepSeek, Mistral, Grok).

Model to use: allows you to choose the exact model from a dropdown menu (e.g.: gpt-4-turbo, claude-3.5, mistral-largeâ€¦).

OpenRouter AI #1, #2, #3, #4, #5

OpenRouter works differently because with a single API Key you can access multiple models. That's why here you have 5 spaces to configure different models at the same time.

  • Use Free Models = TRUE â†’ uses the free model.
  • Use Free Models = FALSE â†’ uses the paid model.
  • Free model selection: choose a free model from the dropdown.
  • Paid model selection: choose a paid model from the dropdown.
ğŸ‘‰ This repeats 5 times: So you can have up to 5 different OpenRouter models, mixing free and paid ones.

ğŸ“Œ Multiple AI Consultation

Enable Multiple AI Consultation

If set to true, allows ARIA to consult multiple AIs at the same time. If set to false, the Select AI Provider parameter will be used.

Individual AI Provider Inclusion

Each provider can be activated (true) or deactivated (false):

  • Include OpenAI in multiple consultation
  • Include Llama in multiple consultation
  • Include Gemini in multiple consultation
  • Include Claude in multiple consultation
  • Include DeepSeek in multiple consultation
  • Include Mistral in multiple consultation
  • Include Grok in multiple consultation
  • Include OpenRouter AI #1 to #5 in multiple consultation

ğŸ—³ï¸ Decision Type for Multiple AIs

Decision Type for Multiple AIs

We have 3 possible decision types:

  • Majority Decision Default = Simple majority (we recommend using this) e.g.: 3/5 AIs agree.
  • Majority Decision Custom = A majority that is customized in the parameter AI Count Required for Majority Custom Mode, example: I have 5 active AIs and I want that for a buy or sell option to be considered, 4 AIs must say sell. Not recommended for free AIs, only for advanced users.
  • Unanimous Decision = Unanimous decision, 5/5 AIs agree.
Recommendation: Use Majority Decision Default for most scenarios. It provides good balance between accuracy and trade frequency.

ğŸ§  XGBoost ML Configuration

Enable XGBoost ML for SL/TP

When set to true, XGBoost takes control of Stop Loss and Take Profit calculations using advanced machine learning algorithms.

XGBoost API URL

Must use exclusively: https://aria-mcp-bridge.onrender.com

This is the official ARIA Audit API endpoint for XGBoost integration. Based on the [ARIA Audit API](https://aria-mcp-bridge.onrender.com), this service provides trade analysis and strategy optimization.

XGBoost Data Path

Default: xgboost\ in MT5 data directory

Local folder path for XGBoost training data files.

  • Used to store historical market data for ML training
  • Contains all files saved by XGBoost learning process
  • Location: MT5 data directory for easy access

Minimum Confidence Level

Default: 0.60 (60%)

Minimum confidence required to use XGBoost prediction.

  • Range: 0.0 (0%) to 1.0 (100%)
  • Higher values = more conservative, fewer false signals
  • Lower values = more aggressive, higher false signals

Use Fallback Mode

Default: ON

Enable fallback when XGBoost API is unavailable.

  • Uses ATR-based calculations as backup method
  • Recommended: ON for continuous trading operation
Backup Strategy: When XGBoost is unavailable, ARIA automatically switches to ATR (Average True Range) calculations to maintain trading operations without interruption.

Debug Mode

Default: OFF

Enable detailed logging for XGBoost operations.

ğŸ§  What is XGBoost and How it Manages SL/TP Levels in ARIA

XGBoost is a statistical mathematical model, pre-trained and widely used for optimizing trading data. It was trained with 60,000 real audited trades that ARIA took live and that have been manually uploaded by users during V3, so it already starts with a knowledge base about ARIA and its trades.

ğŸ“ Learning Process:
  • ğŸ“š Pre-trained Base: Starts with knowledge from all V3 user audits
  • ğŸ“… Daily Learning: Each day at the end of trading hours, XGBoost saves what it learned during the day to its memory
  • ğŸ” Self-Audit: It will self-audit to see what it got wrong, what went well, and what it can improve
  • ğŸ§  Daily Improvement: This process is daily, so each day, it will be a little wiser
ğŸŒ Collective Learning: Since it's a machine learning model, XGBoost learns from all trades of all ARIA users. Therefore, the more different users run ARIA, the faster it will improve.
ğŸ” Total Transparency:

You can always see what it learns and what it saves to memory, both in the Experts tab and in its XGBoost Folder Data Path, for complete transparency.

  • ğŸ“Š Experts Tab: Real-time learning logs and decisions
  • ğŸ“ XGBoost Folder: Stored learning data and model updates
  • ğŸ” Full Visibility: Monitor what the model learns and how it evolves

ğŸ“° News Filter

News Filter Configuration

ARIA connects to https://nfs.faireconomy.media/ to retrieve high and medium impact news related to the symbol it is currently trading.

There's no need to modify anything manually â€” It will automatically detect your broker's time zone.

If news is detected for the symbol, ARIA will not take any new trades, and will pause trading 30 minutes before and 30 minutes after the event.

Enable News Filter

This feature can be enabled by setting "Enable News Filter" to true, or disabled with false if you prefer ARIA to keep trading regardless of news.

News Impact Level Options

You will then have 3 options to choose from:

  • High Impact News (e.g. NFP, FOMC, Interest Rate Decisions)
  • Medium Impact News (e.g. PMI, Retail Sales, Unemployment Claims)
  • Both (High and Medium Impact)
âš ï¸ Keep in mind:
  • If you choose both, you may notice a reduction in the number of trades due to this filter.
  • Ideally, you should only pause trading during high impact news events.
ğŸ†• V4 Visual Indicator: When news events are active for a currency pair and ARIA is not trading due to this filter, the chart frame will appear in red color. If the frame is green, it means the news filter allows trading on that pair because there are no active news events at that moment. If the news filter is disabled, the frame will always appear green since this means the filter "allows" new operations to be opened.
Recommended Setting: Enable filter for High Impact News only to maintain good trade frequency while avoiding major volatility events.

ğŸ“ Fractal Parameters

â“ What is it and what is it for?

It is a confirmation filter by timeframe confluence. Before allowing an operation, ARIA checks that several timeframes "agree" with the direction (bullish or bearish). The more confirmations you ask for, the fewer operations (but of higher quality) the EA will approve.

ğŸ”‘ Key Idea: Confluence = quality. Without confluence or with opposite signals between timeframes, the filter denies entry.

ğŸ† Golden Rules (Very Important)

âš ï¸ Rule #1: Never include the trading timeframe within the fractal filter.
  • Example: If you trade on M5, activate M15 and higher (M15/M30/H1); do not activate M5.
  • Reason: Avoid "self-confirming" and overfitting the signal. Always confirm with higher timeframes.
  • More timeframes = fewer trades (stricter filter)
  • More minimum confirmations = more selective (discards more signals)
  • Recommended: Activate 2 confirmations from higher TFs, as more will lose many trading opportunities
  • Adjust filter to instrument and its volatility (EURUSD â‰  GOLD)

âš™ï¸ Parameters (What they mean and how they affect)

Enable Fractal Filter

Turns on/off the multi-TF confluence system.

Timeframes to Evaluate

Select the timeframes (e.g. M15, M30, H1, H4, D1).

Remember: Only higher than the timeframe where you operate and no more than 2 TF.
Minimum Confirmations

How many of the selected TFs must agree in the same direction to allow entry.

  • 1â€“2 = more operations (more flexible)
  • 3â€“4 = fewer operations (more demanding)
Lookback Periods

How many candles back each TF looks to evaluate fractals/trend.

  • More lookback: More robust signals, but later
  • Less lookback: Faster signals, but more noise
Trend Strength (Threshold)

Minimum "consistency" (e.g., 0.6) that the filter must detect to accept.

  • Higher value: Reduces entries in sideways markets
  • Lower value: More entries, but less selective

ğŸ”§ How to Configure it (Quick Step by Step)

  1. Choose your operating timeframe (e.g.: M5, M15, H1)
  2. Activate the fractal filter
  3. Mark only higher TFs (if you operate M15 â†’ activate M30/H1/H4)
  4. Set "Minimum Confirmations" according to your style (2 or 3)
  5. Adjust Lookback (base 10â€“20 candles per TF) and Strength (0.6 approx.)
  6. Test it on demo
ğŸ’° Token Consumption Warning: Remember that this parameter, when activated and sending various data from different TFs, consumes more tokens. If you are using paid models, check consumption, since if you are on very small TFs consulting every 5 minutes, consumption will skyrocket. It's different if you work from M15 onwards, where consultations are more spaced.

ğŸ“š Practical Reading

More TFs + more confirmations = more filter â†’ fewer entries and higher probability of success in trending markets.

âœ… Clear Examples (Yes/No)

ğŸ”¥ I operate on M5 (scalping):
  • âœ… Yes: M15 + M30 + H1 (min. 2 conf.)
  • âŒ No: activate M5 in the filter (breaks rule #1)
ğŸ“ˆ I operate on M30 (intraday):
  • âœ… Yes: H1 + H4 + D1 (min. 2â€“3 conf.)
  • âŒ No: include M30 in the list

ğŸ”— Interactions with Other Systems

  • With spread and news: The fractal can give "OK", but if the spread is high or there is high impact news, ARIA will block anyway (filters are cumulative).
  • With schedules: Outside your trading window, operation is denied even if confluence is perfect.
  • With risk management: By requiring confluence, it reduces overtrading and stabilizes drawdown.

âŒ Common Errors (and how to avoid them)

Error #1: Include the trading timeframe in the filter â‡’ No (rule #1). You will block almost everything or self-confirm.
Error #2: Activate too many TFs with many confirmations (e.g. 5 TF and ask for 4) â‡’ you run out of operations. Start with 2â€“3 TF with 2 conf. and increase if necessary.
Error #3: Use the same preset for all symbols â‡’ GOLD/indices require more relaxed configurations (high volatility).
Error #4: Very short lookback â‡’ "fragile" signals and more noise; too long â‡’ you arrive late. Start at 10â€“20.

â¸ï¸ Cooldown

â“ What is it and what does it solve?

The Cooldown is an automatic pause between operations to avoid over-trading right after an SL or TP. During that window, ARIA does not open new positions (according to your configuration), which helps to cut streaks, reduce "revenge trading" and let the market stabilize before the next trade.

ğŸ¯ Main Benefits:
  • ğŸ›‘ Prevents over-trading after SL/TP events
  • ğŸ˜¤ Reduces revenge trading impulses
  • ğŸ“Š Market stabilization time
  • ğŸ“‰ Cuts losing streaks

âš™ï¸ Where it's configured and what parameters it has

In the Filters/Systems panel you will see the Cooldown controls:

  • Enable Cooldown: activates/deactivates the system
  • Cooldown Minutes: duration of the pause (e.g., 1â€“180 min)
  • Apply on SL: if cooldown is triggered when closing by Stop Loss
  • Apply on TP: if cooldown is triggered when closing by Take Profit
  • Per Symbol (per-symbol): cooldown affects only the instrument of that closure; if deactivated, cooldown can be global
ğŸ“Œ Note: Filters in ARIA are cumulative. Even if Cooldown "lets a trade pass", other filters (spread, news, schedules, fractal, etc.) can block it and vice versa.

ğŸ”„ How it Works (Real Flow)

  1. Position closes by SL and/or TP (according to what you marked)
  2. ARIA registers the event and starts the cooldown countdown
  3. While cooldown is active, no new operations are launched from the chosen scope (symbol or global)
  4. Time completed, the system becomes available again without you having to do anything
Example Flow:

EURUSD trade closes with SL â†’ 30-minute cooldown starts â†’ No new EURUSD trades â†’ Timer expires â†’ Normal trading resumes

âœ… Practical Benefits

  • ğŸ¯ Controls impulse to re-enter immediately after an SL or large TP
  • ğŸŒŠ Avoids "accelerated" markets after a breakout or news, when spread/volatility has not yet normalized
  • ğŸ“Š Stabilizes drawdown and lowers variance by spacing decisions

ğŸ”— Important Interactions

With Other Filters
  • Spread / News / Schedules: If any of these filters is blocking, cooldown doesn't "force" anything; the trade still doesn't pass. Think of cooldown as another layer of temporal security.
With Overtrading Control
  • Complementary systems: Cooldown cuts by time; anti-overtrading cuts by time and/or price distance
  • Double lock: Use them together when the market is "nervous"
With Profit/Loss Limits
  • Priority system: If you reach a daily limit and the EA is paused, the limit pause takes priority; cooldown is secondary
Multi-Symbol Trading
  • Per Symbol active: You can have EURUSD in cooldown and continue operating GBPUSD
  • Global: Everything stops

âŒ Common Errors (and how to avoid them)

Error #1: Minutes too low â†’ doesn't avoid market over-reaction. Increase gradually and test on demo.
Error #2: Only TP or only SL when your strategy needs both. If you see streaks after any closure, enable both triggers.
Error #3: Global unintentionally: if you operate multiple symbols, activate per symbol to not freeze the entire setup.
Error #4: "Never operates": sometimes it's not the cooldown but other filters (spread, news, schedules). Check the status panel to see which filter blocked the trade.

ğŸ¯ TP to Breakeven

â“ What is TP to Breakeven?

It is a hybrid function between take profit and breakeven.

The logic is: when the price reaches a certain partial TP level, the EA automatically moves the SL to the entry price (or with a small positive margin).

ğŸ“Š Practical Example:
  1. You open a buy on EURUSD at 1.1000
  2. You configure TP-to-BE at +30 pips
  3. When price reaches 1.1030, the EA moves your SL from 1.1000 â†’ 1.1005 (5 pips secured profit)
  4. This way you lock partial profit and prevent the operation from going negative

âš™ï¸ Configuration Parameters

In ARIA it appears as "TP â†’ BE" system and depends on parameters like:

  • Activation Distance (pips): How many pips profit needed to trigger
  • Offset (additional pips): Extra pips above entry price for safety
  • Activation Conditions: Always after a mini-TP is reached
ğŸ¯ Use Case: Perfect for scalping and intraday strategies where you want to secure partial profits quickly.

ğŸ”’ Breakeven

â“ What is Breakeven?

Simpler system: when the trade advances in favor X pips, the EA moves the SL to exact entry price (or entry + offset).

Ensures that the operation does not close at a loss, but without needing to reach the TP.

ğŸ“Š Example:
  1. Buy at 1.1000
  2. Breakeven activated at +20 pips
  3. When price touches 1.1020, SL moves to 1.1000
  4. Result: Either you win or exit without loss

âš ï¸ Important Compatibility Note

âš ï¸ Warning: In ARIA it is not recommended to use Breakeven and Trailing at the same time, because both try to move the SL and enter into conflict.

ğŸ“ˆ Trailing Options

1. Trailing OFF

  • The system is deactivated
  • ARIA will not move the Stop Loss automatically
  • Only managed with fixed SL, fixed TP, TPâ†’BE or AI management, according to what you have active

2. Trailing in Pips

It is the classic trailing, based on distance in pips.

Main Parameters:
  • Start: how many pips profit the trade must advance for it to activate
  • Step: every how many pips the SL will be updated
  • Distance: the constant separation it will maintain with respect to the current price
ğŸ“Œ Example:
  • Buy EURUSD at 1.1000
  • Trailing Start = 20 pips, Distance = 15
  • When it reaches 1.1020 â†’ activates and SL rises to 1.1005
  • At 1.1030 â†’ SL rises to 1.1015
  • And so on...
âœ… Useful for: Stable pairs with "clean" movements (EURUSD, GBPUSD).

3. Trailing in Percent (RECOMMENDED)

Instead of pips, it is based on a percentage of floating profit.

1. Trailing Start (0.05)

Defines from what percentage of floating profit the trailing is activated.

  • Example: 0.05 = 5%
  • When the operation reaches +5% profit relative to risk/position, dynamic trailing is activated
2. Trailing Stop (0.025)

Indicates the minimum percentage of profit that is secured once trailing is active.

  • Example: 0.025 = 2.5%
  • Even if the market retraces, the EA will move the Stop Loss to always have at least +2.5% of the operation secured
3. Trailing Step (0.01)

Defines how often the trailing is adjusted, expressed as additional percentage.

  • Example: 0.01 = 1%
  • For every +1% extra that the price advances, the SL will be readjusted to maintain the security proportion
ğŸ“Š Practical Example with these values:

Suppose an operation opens and profit begins to grow:

  • +3% profit â†’ Nothing happens, trailing not yet active
  • +5% profit â†’ Trailing activates. SL moves to guarantee +2.5%
  • +6% profit â†’ SL adjusts again (1% Step). Now secures +3.5% approx.
  • +7% profit â†’ SL rises again. Secures +4.5%, and so on

ğŸ”„ Key Difference vs. Trailing Pips

Comparison:
  • In pips: Everything is fixed: distance in price points
  • In percent: Everything is dynamic: depends on how much the operation is winning

This makes Trailing Percent ideal for very volatile assets (GOLD, BTC, indices), because it automatically adapts to the movement.

ğŸ“Š System Comparison Table

System When it activates How it protects Typical use
TP â†’ BE When touching a mini-TP Secures partial profit and eliminates risk Scalping or intraday strategies
Breakeven When advancing X pips in favor Eliminates risk (no loss, no extra profit secured) Conservative strategies
Trailing When exceeding a pip threshold Locks more and more profit following the price Swing or strong trends

âš ï¸ Compatibility

âœ… Compatible:
  • TP â†’ BE + Trailing: Can be used together, because TP-BE secures the first protection and then Trailing follows the price
âŒ Not Compatible:
  • Breakeven + Trailing: NOT compatible, generate technical conflicts

ğŸ“Š Support/Resistance Filter

â“ What is it for?

The Support/Resistance (S/R) filter avoids entering just against a relevant technical level (ceiling/floor). If the price is too close to a resistance (for buys) or to a support (for sells), it blocks the operation. It can also let breakouts pass when the separation exceeds your tolerance.

ğŸ¯ Key Logic:
  • ğŸ›‘ Blocks entries against strong S/R levels
  • ğŸš€ Allows breakouts when price moves beyond tolerance
  • ğŸ“Š Technical protection against bad entries

ğŸ” How ARIA Determines S/R (User View)

  1. Looks at candle history (lookback) and detects candidate levels
  2. Only considers confirmed levels with a minimum of "touches" (retest)
  3. Uses ATR-based tolerance to count those touches as valid (doesn't require exact price to the pip)
  4. Evaluates if your entry would be too close to the level: if yes, blocks; if not, allows (or interprets as possible breakout)
ğŸ”‘ Key Idea: More touches = stronger level. Lower tolerance = stricter filter.

âš™ï¸ Parameters in the Panel

Enable S/R Filter

Activates/deactivates the filter.

Lookback Periods

How many candles it uses to search for levels (e.g., 50).

  • More lookback: Finds "historical" stronger levels (but fewer signals)
  • Less lookback: More recent levels, more signals
Min Touches

How many times the level must have been "touched" to consider it valid (e.g., 3).

  • More touches: More reliable level â†’ more selective filter
  • Fewer touches: More levels detected, less selective
Touch Tolerance (% ATR)

Margin to consider that a touch was "at the same level".

  • High tolerance: Encompasses more touches (more valid levels, stricter filter)
  • Low tolerance: Requires more precise touches
Use High/Low vs Use Close
  • Use High/Low: Validates levels with candle highs/lows (more purist)
  • Use Close: Validates levels with closes (more conservative with long wicks)
ğŸ“Œ Base Recommendation: Use High/Low = ON to detect "real" ceilings/floors; activate Use Close only if your instrument has very noisy wicks (indices, crypto).

ğŸ§  How the Filter "Thinks" When Deciding

  • Buy: If entry price falls within tolerance of a confirmed resistance, blocks (you're buying "below the ceiling")
  • Sell: If price is within tolerance of a support, blocks (you'd be selling "above the floor")
  • Breakouts: If your price is beyond level + tolerance (buy above broken resistance / sell below broken support), lets pass and considers valid breakout

ğŸ”— Important Interactions

With Automatic Modes (Time / Breakout / Trend-Follow)

In Breakout/Trend-Follow, S/R is gold: confirms you're breaking (or respecting) levels, avoiding entries against the level.

With Other Filters

All filters are cumulative: even if S/R "lets pass", high Spread or News can still block.

With Trailing/Breakeven/TPâ†’BE

S/R only decides entry. Management (trailing, BE, TPâ†’BE) operates after and doesn't interfere with S/R.

âš ï¸ Overfiltering: If you combine Fractal + S/R + Hours + News with strict parameters, it's normal for frequency to drop a lot; adjust one at a time.

âŒ Common Errors (and how to avoid them)

Error #1: Very short lookback â†’ detects weak/random levels. Increase to 50â€“60 candles (majors) or 60â€“80 (volatiles).
Error #2: Min Touches too high â†’ almost no valid levels â†’ too many entries (because it "doesn't see" the level) or none (if tolerance is also large).
Error #3: Very low tolerance on volatile instruments â†’ system "doesn't see" legitimate touches and underestimates levels.
Error #4: Using Close = OFF on assets with long wicks â†’ filter becomes too "nervous"; consider Close = ON.
Error #5: Not checking symbol's ATR â†’ tolerance in % ATR loses meaning if ATR doesn't adjust to the timeframe you use.

ğŸ“ Spread Filter

ğŸ¯ Spread Filter Objective

This filter is one of the most practical protections the system has, because it directly controls the cost of entering the market.

The spread is the difference between Bid and Ask price. When it widens too much (brokers in low liquidity, dead hours or strong news), entering at that moment is almost always disadvantageous.

The Spread Filter:
  • ğŸš« Blocks trade opening if spread exceeds the limit you configure
  • ğŸ“Š Optionally uses spread average to avoid false blocks by momentary spikes

âš™ï¸ Spread Filter Parameters

Enable Spread Filter

Activates or deactivates the filter.

Max Spread (in pips)

Maximum allowed value. Example: 3.0 pips on EURUSD.

If current spread is greater â†’ EA does not open operation.

Use Average

If activated, doesn't take a single tick, but the average spread over a period.

This avoids blocks by half-second micro-spikes.

Average Periods

Number of candles/periods used to calculate that average.

Typical example: 10 periods.

ğŸ§  How it Works in Practice

  1. EA measures spread in real time
  2. If value exceeds your allowed maximum, entry signal is discarded even if AIs give "Buy/Sell"
  3. If you have average activated, compares against average of last X periods
  4. If spread returns to normal â†’ system allows entries again

âœ… Benefits

  • ğŸ›¡ï¸ Protection against brokers in low liquidity hours
  • ğŸ“° Avoids operations in news with 5x or 10x larger spread
  • ğŸ“Š Improves result consistency, because you don't pay exaggerated entry costs
  • ğŸ¤ Complements very well News Filter and Trading Hours

âŒ Common Errors

Error #1: Configure maximum spread too low:
  • Example: 1.0 pip on GOLD (where normal is 8â€“15)
  • Result: EA almost never enters
Error #2: Configure too high:
  • Example: 10 pips on EURUSD
  • Result: Enters at times when cost is prohibitive
Error #3: Not activating average on pairs with frequent micro-spikes â†’ false blocks.

ğŸ¤– AutoTrading

AutomodeEnabled = true / false

This parameter defines whether ARIA operates automatically or only manually:

âœ… AutomodeEnabled = true

  • EA analyzes, consults AIs and opens operations by itself when conditions are met
  • Complete automated flow: AI + filters + risk management works without intervention
  • Normal mode for automatic trading

âŒ AutomodeEnabled = false

  • EA does not open new operations by itself
  • But it does manage those you open manually (from Panel or from MT5):
  • Dynamic SL/TP
  • Breakeven / Trailing / TPâ†’BE
  • AI closures (if you allow it)
  • Ideal when you want to use ARIA as advanced manager and not as 100% automatic system

âš™ï¸ Trading Mode

Trading Mode (3 available options)

ARIA has three entry logic modes, which define how it interprets signals and filters opportunities:

ğŸ•’ a) Time Mode

Operates at fixed time intervals, according to the frequency you configure (e.g. every 15 min, every 1 hour).

At each interval, ARIA makes a query to the AIs and decides whether to open or not.

  • âœ… Advantage: Total control over operation frequency and AI costs
  • âŒ Disadvantage: May give entries even if there's no strong technical event (just by "time turn")
  • ğŸ‘‰ Used a lot in: Scalping and intraday

ğŸ’¥ b) Breakout Mode

Designed to operate key level breakouts (support/resistance, consolidations).

EA waits for price to exit a range and consults AIs if the breakout has real strength.

  • âœ… Advantage: Captures explosive movements (news, range breaks)
  • âŒ Disadvantage: Fewer operations, more sensitive to false breakouts if you don't calibrate tolerance and filters well
  • ğŸ‘‰ Very useful in: Volatile pairs, GOLD, BTC, indices

ğŸ“ˆ c) Trend Follow Mode

Only seeks to enter in favor of the main trend.

Uses direction filters (MAs, fractal, AI) to ensure not going against the major flow.

  • âœ… Advantage: High probability operations in trending contexts
  • âŒ Disadvantage: In sideways ranges can give very few signals or enter late
  • ğŸ‘‰ Ideal for: Swing trading and letting long trends run

âš ï¸ Important Notes

Single Mode Only: You can only have 1 trading mode active at a time.

The Spread Filter, News, S/R, Fractal, Cooldown, etc. apply equally in any of the three modes (filters are cumulative).

ğŸ”„ Combination Examples:
  • AutomodeEnabled = false + Trading Mode = Trend Follow â†’ only manages manual trades that go in favor of the trend
  • AutomodeEnabled = true + Trading Mode = Breakout â†’ 100% automatic system, focused only on breakouts

â±ï¸ Frequency Parameters

â“ What do they control?

They control how often ARIA consults the AI to analyze the market and decide whether to open an operation.

They are normally expressed in minutes.

ğŸ“Š Examples:
  • Frequency = 15 min â†’ EA asks the AI every 15 minutes
  • Frequency = 60 min â†’ Once per hour

âš–ï¸ Frequency Impact

âš ï¸ Lower Frequency (More Often)

  • ğŸ“ˆ More potential operations
  • ğŸ’¸ More API consumption (cost)

âš ï¸ Higher Frequency (Less Often)

  • ğŸ“‰ Fewer operations
  • ğŸ’° Less AI cost
ğŸ‘‰ Recommendation: Calibrate based on trading style (scalping = lower, swing = higher).

ğŸ¯ Confidence to Trade

â“ What is it?

It is the minimum confidence level (%) that ARIA requires in the AI response to execute an operation.

ğŸ“Š Example:
  • Confidence = 70% â†’ if AI returns Buy with 65% confidence, EA does NOT open
  • If it returns Buy with 82%, EA does open

âš–ï¸ Confidence Impact

  • Higher values = fewer operations but more quality
  • Lower values = more operations but more noise and risk
ğŸ‘‰ Typical Range: 60â€“75%
  • Scalping: Better higher (70â€“75%)
  • Swing: You can try something lower (60â€“65%) to not lose long-term opportunities

ğŸ’° Lot Management Parameters

â“ What does it define?

Here you define how the EA calculates the lot size of each operation. You have 3 modes:

a) Dynamic (Risk Based) â­ RECOMMENDED

The lot is calculated according to a risk % on your balance/equity and the SL distance.

ğŸ“Š Example (as in your image):
  • Dynamic Risk Percentage = 2.0
  • This means each operation will risk 2% of your account up to the Stop Loss
  • If your balance is $1,000, and SL = 100 pips â†’ lot will be necessary so that, if it hits SL, you lose $20 (2%)
âœ… It's the most professional method, automatically adapts lot to risk.

b) Fixed

You use a fixed lot always.

Example: Lot Value = 1.0 â†’ always opens with 1.0 lot regardless of balance or SL.
  • âœ… Useful for: Simple backtests
  • âŒ Dangerous on small accounts, because it doesn't scale risk

c) Percentage (Lot Scaling)

The lot is calculated as a % of total balance, not based on SL.

ğŸ“Š Example:
  • Lot Value = 2 â†’ means it opens a lot equivalent to 2% of balance
  • Balance $1,000 â†’ lot = 0.02
  • Balance $10,000 â†’ lot = 0.20
  • âœ… Scales with balance
  • âŒ Doesn't consider SL distance â†’ real risk can vary

âš™ï¸ Where to place each value according to the Lot you use

Configuration Example:
  • Lot Value = 1.0 (this value is ignored in Dynamic; would only be used in Fixed or Percentage)
  • Dynamic Risk Percentage = 2.0 â†’ Each operation will risk 2% of your account up to the Stop Loss

Example: balance $5,000 â†’ maximum risk $100 per trade.

ğŸ¯ SL/TP Parameters

â“ What do they configure?

Here you configure how Stop Loss (SL) and Take Profit (TP) levels are calculated and placed.

Both SL and TP have their own calculation mode and an associated value.

âš™ï¸ SL Mode and TP Mode Options

ğŸ“Š Percentage

SL or TP calculated as a % of price or balance.

Example: SL = 1% â†’ if balance is $10,000, maximum risk will be $100.

It's a mode proportional to account size.

ğŸ“ Fixed Pips

Fixed SL or TP in pips.

Example: SL = 30 â†’ always places a Stop at 30 pips distance from entry.

It's a rigid system (doesn't adapt to volatility).

ğŸ¤– AI Recommendation

SL/TP levels are suggested by AI after analyzing market situation.

Example: AI can suggest SL at a relevant support and TP at the next resistance.

Very dynamic, but depends on AI connection stability.

ğŸ“Š Swing ATR

Calculates SL/TP based on ATR (Average True Range) of the timeframe.

Example: ATR = 50 pips on H1; if you configure multiplier = 2, SL = 100 pips.

Adapts to current asset volatility.

ğŸ§  XGBoost Machine Learning (Advanced Mode from V4)
âš ï¸ Important: Must have activated in the parameter Enable XGBoost ML for SL/TP = True to allow connection.

The XGBoost model evaluates volatility, market structure and historical results to dynamically optimize SL and TP.

ğŸ“ Learning Process:
  • ğŸ“š Learns with each operation: adjusts levels better after hits/misses
  • ğŸ§  Most "intelligent" option: evolutionary system
  • ğŸ“ˆ Daily improvement: refines decisions each day

âš™ï¸ Associated Parameters

SL Parameter Value (in PIPS)
  • If mode is Fixed Pips: here you define exact pips (e.g. 30)
  • If mode is ATR: here you define the multiplier (e.g. 2 Ã— ATR)
  • If it's Percentage: here you define the % (e.g. 1%)
  • In AI or XGBoost mode: this value is not taken into account
TP Parameter Value (in PIPS)

Same logic as SL: defines distance or multiplier according to chosen mode.

Example: TP Mode = Fixed Pips, TP Value = 60 â†’ always places a Take Profit at 60 pips.

ğŸš€ XGBoost Mode Summary

When you are with SL and TP in XGBoost mode, you are in a 100% dynamic mode, where ARIA adjusts SL and TP according to XGBoost learning and current market conditions.

ğŸ“ Continuous Improvement: Keep in mind that each day it will improve and refine its decisions.
ğŸ§  XGBoost Advantages:
  • ğŸ“Š Market Structure Analysis: Considers current volatility and patterns
  • ğŸ“š Historical Learning: Based on 58,000 real audited trades
  • ğŸ”„ Daily Evolution: Self-improves with each trading session
  • ğŸ¯ Optimized Levels: Dynamic SL/TP based on ML predictions

âš–ï¸ AI Risk-Reward Ratio

â“ What is AI RISK-REWARD RATIO?

The AI RISK-REWARD RATIO CONFIGURATION parameter in ARIA Connector EA refers to the system that allows defining the risk-reward relationship (SL/TP) that the AI must respect when suggesting or executing operations.

ğŸ” How it works

  1. User establishes a fixed ratio between Stop Loss (SL) and Take Profit (TP)
  2. Example: 1:2 means that if SL is at 50 pips, TP will automatically be at 100 pips
  3. When this system is activated, AI doesn't suggest arbitrary values, but must always adjust to that preconfigured proportion
  4. AI analyzes market conditions and adapts levels to that framework, verifying they are coherent with supports, resistances and volatility

âš™ï¸ Main Parameters

  • SL Ratio: Risk part. (E.g.: 1 in a 1:2 ratio)
  • TP Ratio: Reward part. (E.g.: 2 in a 1:2 ratio)
  • Use Ratio System: Activates or deactivates this logic
ğŸ“Š Ratio Examples:
  • 1:1 â†’ Conservative (equal risk and reward)
  • 1:2 â†’ Balanced (risk 50 pips, reward 100 pips)
  • 1:3 â†’ Aggressive (risk 30 pips, reward 90 pips)

ğŸ§  AI Flexibility

âš ï¸ Important: This parameter will be respected if the AIs find that ratio viable. If they don't see that ratio as possible but do see a good trade opportunity, they will recommend a different ratio.
ğŸ¯ Smart Adaptation: AI prioritizes good trading opportunities over rigid ratios, ensuring you don't miss profitable trades due to inflexible risk-reward requirements.

ğŸš« Overtrade Control

â“ What is overtrading?

Opening too many operations in a short time or too close to each other. This multiplies risk, generates negative correlation (all operations can lose together) and triggers unnecessary commissions/spreads.

The OVERTRADE CONTROL PARAMETERS block in ARIA Connector EA is designed to avoid overtrading, one of the most common errors that leads to excessive losses.

âš™ï¸ Main System Parameters

Check Existing Positions

Prevents the EA from opening multiple operations on the same symbol simultaneously.

With this, each pair/asset will only have one active position at a time.

Minimum Time Between Trades (seconds)

Defines how much time must pass between closing a trade and opening the next one.

Example: 60 seconds â†’ EA waits at least 1 minute before operating that instrument again.
Minimum Distance in Pips

Prevents opening a new operation too close to the previous one in terms of price.

Example: 50 pips â†’ if there's already a trade on EURUSD at 1.1000, the next one won't open until price is at least at 1.1050 or 1.0950.

âœ… Benefits of Overtrading Control

  • ğŸ›¡ï¸ Reduces overexposure risk
  • ğŸ¯ Avoids "clusters" of entries at the same price level
  • ğŸ˜¤ Protects against emotional trading (like trying to quickly recover a loss)
  • ğŸ“ˆ Increases average trade quality, because it forces waiting for better setups

âš ï¸ Important Warnings

Too Strict Settings:
  • Example: 1 trade per hour and 100 pips separation
  • Result: EA almost never operates
Too Lax Settings:
  • Example: 5 seconds and 5 pips
  • Result: Filter has no real effect
ğŸ“Š Instrument-Specific Adjustment: It's recommended to adjust according to instrument: quiet pairs like EURUSD require fewer filters than very volatile assets like GOLD or GBPJPY.

ğŸ”§ Configuration Guidelines

ğŸ“Š Recommended Settings by Asset:
  • EURUSD/GBPUSD: 30-60 seconds, 20-30 pips
  • GOLD/XAUUSD: 60-120 seconds, 50-100 pips
  • Crypto/Indices: 120-300 seconds, 100-200 pips

ğŸ”„ Mid-Trade AI Query Enable

â“ What is Mid-Trade AI Query?

Function: If set to true, AI will continue making queries even with operations already open.

Objective: Allow AI to recommend moving SL/TP, partial close, or early exit from a trade.

ğŸ¯ Configuration Recommendations

ğŸ”’ FALSE (Default) - Recommended
  • ğŸ›¡ï¸ Safer and simpler
  • âš ï¸ Conflict prevention: This parameter generates conflicts with several other ARIA filters
  • ğŸ‘¥ Target users: Automated traders who prefer set-and-forget approach
  • âœ… Best for: Users who want to avoid parameter conflicts
ğŸ”“ TRUE - Advanced Users Only
  • ğŸ¯ Dynamic management: AI can adjust trades in real-time
  • âš ï¸ Incompatible with: Breakeven and Trailing Stop
  • ğŸ‘¥ Target users: Manual traders who want AI assistance during trades
  • ğŸ”§ Requirements: Must disable Breakeven and Trailing systems

âš ï¸ Important Conflicts

ğŸš« Cannot be used together:
  • Mid-Trade AI Query = TRUE
  • + Breakeven System
  • + Trailing Stop System

Reason: These systems compete for trade management control, causing unpredictable behavior.

ğŸ”’ Hidden SL/TP Enable

â“ What is Hidden SL/TP?

Function: Hides Stop Loss (SL) and Take Profit (TP) levels from the broker.

Objective: Prevent some brokers from doing "stop hunting" (hunting your levels).

How it works: EA saves levels internally and closes the operation when price touches them.

âš ï¸ Important Warnings

ğŸ”Œ Connection Risk:
  • If MT5 disconnects, broker won't see those levels
  • Safety SL and TP will still be active as backup
  • But main hidden levels become inactive during disconnection
ğŸ‘¨â€ğŸ’» Advanced Users Only:
  • Requires understanding of MT5 disconnection risks
  • Only activate if you suspect broker manipulation
  • Not recommended for beginners

ğŸš« System Conflicts

ğŸ”’ Hidden SL/TP Limitations:
âŒ Hidden SL/TP + Mid-Trade AI Query
  • Problem: Mid-Trade queries AI about "visible" SL/TP
  • Issue: If hidden, desynchronization risk
  • Result: AI analyzes different levels than EA manages
âŒ Hidden SL/TP + Trailing Stop
  • Problem: Trailing wants to move SL on server
  • Issue: If hidden, EA manages internally
  • Result: Misalignments, unexpected closes, or execution failures
âŒ Hidden SL/TP + Breakeven
  • Problem: Breakeven wants to move SL to entry point
  • Issue: If hidden, EA must do it virtually
  • Result: Control duplication and possible errors

âœ… Best Practice Conclusion

ğŸ¯ Recommended Usage:
  • Use Hidden SL/TP only if you want to hide levels from broker
  • Keep disabled: Mid-Trade, Trailing, and Breakeven
  • Alternative: If you want dynamic management (Trailing/Breakeven), set Hidden = false

ğŸ“ˆ Additional Timeframe Analysis

ğŸ” Additional Timeframe Enable

ğŸŸ¢ Bullish Engulfing H4 Enable

â“ What is Bullish Engulfing H4?

This parameter activates an additional filter based on a Japanese candlestick pattern: Bullish Engulfing detected on H4 timeframe.

ğŸ“Š Bullish Engulfing Pattern: A bullish candle that completely engulfs the previous bearish candle, indicating potential upward reversal.

ğŸ” How It Works

  1. ğŸ“ˆ H4 Analysis: EA analyzes 4-hour (H4) candles
  2. ğŸ¯ Pattern Detection: When it detects a Bullish Engulfing pattern
  3. ğŸ“ˆ BUY Only: Will only allow BUY entries
  4. âœ… Extra Confirmation: Serves as additional confirmation of bullish strength in market

âœ… Advantages

  • ğŸ¯ Filters BUY entries in zones of possible bullish reversal
  • ğŸ“Š Reinforces success probability by confirming classic reversal pattern
  • ğŸ“ˆ Multi-timeframe validation: Useful for swing trading or when operating on lower timeframes (M15, H1) but wanting H4 validation
  • ğŸ” Classic pattern recognition: Based on proven Japanese candlestick analysis

âš ï¸ Limitations

ğŸš« BUY Only Filter:
  • Only affects BUY operations, not SELL operations
  • No sense activating if you only trade sells or neutral strategies
ğŸ“‰ Reduced Frequency:
  • Reduces number of trades, as pattern doesn't appear frequently
  • May miss bullish movements that don't have this prior pattern
â±ï¸ H4 Dependency:
  • Depends on H4 candle formation
  • May delay entries waiting for pattern confirmation

ğŸ¯ Configuration Summary

âœ… Bullish Engulfing H4 Enable = TRUE

âŒ Bullish Engulfing H4 Enable = FALSE

Result: EA ignores this filter and doesn't require pattern confirmation

ğŸ“Š Usage Recommendations

ğŸ¯ Activate when:
  • You focus primarily on BUY trades
  • You want additional reversal confirmation
  • You prefer quality over quantity in entries
  • You're swing trading or position trading
ğŸš« Don't activate when:
  • You trade both directions equally
  • You focus on SELL trades
  • You want maximum trade frequency
  • You're scalping on very low timeframes

ğŸ’° Profit/Loss Limits

â“ What does this parameter control?

It's a global profit or loss limit.

Unlike the SL/TP per trade calculated by ARIA XGBoost, this parameter applies to the entire trading session (day, week, or active cycle).

ğŸ“Š Key Difference:
  • Individual SL/TP: Calculated by ARIA XGBoost per trade
  • Global Limits: Apply to accumulated results across all trades in session

ğŸ¯ How It Works

ğŸ“ˆ Profit Limit

Function: If you reach certain level of accumulated gains â†’ EA stops opening new operations.

Purpose: Protect profits and avoid giving back gains in overtrading.

ğŸ“‰ Loss Limit

Function: If you reach certain level of accumulated losses â†’ EA cuts the session to protect capital.

Purpose: Damage control and capital preservation.

âš™ï¸ Step-by-Step Configuration

ğŸ’š Profit Limit Setup
  1. Enable Profit Limit = true
    • Activates global profit control
    • Example: if you set 1000, when EA earns $1000 (accumulated across multiple operations), it stops opening more trades
  2. Profit Limit Type = Fixed Amount in Money
    • Indicates limit is in money (not percentage or pips)
    • Generally used in USD or account base currency
  3. Profit Limit Amount = X
    • Here you define the profit threshold
    • Example: 1000.0 â†’ session closes with $1000 profit
ğŸ”´ Loss Limit Setup
  1. Enable Loss Limit = true
    • Activates global loss control
    • Very important to protect yourself from bad days
  2. Loss Limit Type = Fixed Amount in Money
    • Same as profit: limit expressed in money
    • Absolute value (positive number representing loss)
  3. Loss Limit Amount = X
    • Here you define maximum you're willing to lose in a day or session
    • Example: 500.0 â†’ if you lose $500, EA stops automatically

ğŸ¯ Real Usage Example

ğŸ“Š Configuration Example:
  • Profit Limit: $1000
  • Loss Limit: $500
  • Starting Balance: $10,000
ğŸ“ˆ Scenario A: Profit Limit Reached
  • Result: You earn $1020 total
  • Action: EA stops opening trades
  • Benefit: Protects accumulated gains
  • Status: Successful session preserved
ğŸ“‰ Scenario B: Loss Limit Reached
  • Result: You lose $520 total
  • Action: EA stops immediately
  • Benefit: Prevents further losses
  • Status: Damage controlled

ğŸ’¡ Best Practices

ğŸ¯ Recommended Ratios:
  • Conservative: Profit Limit 2:1 Loss Limit (e.g., $1000 profit, $500 loss)
  • Balanced: Profit Limit 1.5:1 Loss Limit (e.g., $750 profit, $500 loss)
  • Aggressive: Profit Limit 1:1 Loss Limit (e.g., $500 profit, $500 loss)
âš ï¸ Important Considerations:
  • Account Size: Limits should be proportional to account balance
  • Risk Tolerance: Never risk more than you can afford to lose
  • Session Reset: Limits typically reset daily or per trading session
  • Existing Trades: EA may close existing trades when limits are reached

â° Trading Hours Control

â“ What do trading hours control?

Trading hours parameters allow you to restrict when the EA can open new positions, providing precise control over your trading schedule and market exposure.

ğŸ¯ Main Functions

ğŸ”’ Operation Opening Restriction
  • Active hours: EA only opens trades within defined time range
  • Outside hours: No new entries (but can close existing trades)
  • Flexibility: Existing positions can be managed regardless of time
ğŸ“… Weekly Management
  • Day selection: Activate or deactivate trading by day of week
  • Examples: Avoid Sundays or Friday afternoons
  • Custom schedules: Different hours for different days
ğŸŒ Broker Server Synchronization
  • âš ï¸ Very important: Hours are NOT your local time nor your VPS time
  • Server time: Uses your MT5 broker server time!!
  • Timezone awareness: Must account for broker's timezone

âš™ï¸ Typical Parameters Configuration

ğŸ”§ Basic Settings
Enable Trading Hours Control

Options: TRUE/FALSE

Function: Activate or deactivate time filter

Default: Usually FALSE (no time restrictions)

Close All Trades at Time End

Options: TRUE/FALSE

Function: If TRUE, closes all trades when session ends

Risk: May close profitable trades prematurely

Enable Weekend Trading

Options: TRUE/FALSE

Function: Allow or block weekend trades

Note: Most forex markets closed on weekends

â° Time Configuration
Trading Start Hour

Format: HH:MM (24-hour format)

Example: 09:00 (session start time)

Trading End Hour

Format: HH:MM (24-hour format)

Example: 18:00 (session end time)

ğŸ“… Daily Parameters (Monday - Sunday)
ğŸ“Š Individual Day Configuration:
  • Start Hour/Minute: When trading starts for that specific day
  • End Hour/Minute: When trading stops for that specific day
  • Enable/Disable: Turn trading on/off for specific days

ğŸŒ Timezone Considerations

âš ï¸ Critical Timezone Note: These schedules are typically set using the broker's server timezone (often GMT+2 or GMT+3). If your broker uses a different timezone, you must adjust accordingly.
ğŸ• Timezone Adjustment Example:
  • Default setting: GMT+3
  • Your broker: GMT-3
  • Adjustment needed: Subtract 6 hours from default times
  • Result: If default is 09:00, set 03:00 for your broker

A unique number for trades opened by the EA in automatic mode.

ğŸ¯ Usage

Allows separating management of 100% automatic trades.

ğŸ”§ Step-by-Step Debugging Process

ğŸ¯ Systematic Approach

  4. âš™ï¸ Test with Minimal Configuration

    • Use single AI with 65% confidence
    • Test during active market hours
  5. ğŸ“ˆ Monitor for 30 Minutes
    • Let EA run with simplified settings
    • Watch Experts tab for activity
    • Gradually re-enable filters one by one

âš ï¸ Common Blocking Scenarios

ğŸš« Why ARIA Might Not Trade

ğŸ• Time-Related Blocks
  • Outside trading hours: EA configured for different timezone
  • Weekend trading disabled: Trying to trade on Saturday/Sunday
  • News events: Major economic announcements blocking trades
ğŸ“Š Market Condition Blocks
  • High spread: Spread exceeds maximum allowed
  • Low volatility: Market too quiet for configured thresholds
  • High volatility: Market too chaotic for safe entry
ğŸ¤– AI-Related Blocks
  • Low AI confidence: All AI responses below minimum threshold
  • AI recommends WAIT: No clear directional signal
  • Multiple AI disagreement: No consensus in voting system
ğŸ”§ Technical Blocks
  • Insufficient margin: Account can't open new positions
  • Existing positions: Overtrade control preventing new entries
  • Profit/Loss limits: Daily limits already reached

Conflicts

âš ï¸ Incompatibilities

Critical parameter conflicts and compatibility issues you must avoid in ARIA V4.

ğŸš¨ Warning: These combinations can cause system malfunctions, unexpected behavior, or complete EA failure. Always check these incompatibilities before configuring your EA.

ğŸš¨ Critical Problems

âŒ Trailing Stop + Breakeven

ğŸ”§ The Problem

Both systems want to move the Stop Loss (SL).

âš ï¸ Conflict Details
  • Breakeven: Wants to move SL to entry point
  • Trailing Stop: Wants to move SL continuously following price
  • Result: System doesn't work correctly - competing controls
ğŸš« Never Use Together: Choose either Trailing Stop OR Breakeven, never both simultaneously.

âŒ Mid-Trade Queries + Trailing/Breakeven

ğŸ”§ The Problem

Mid-Trade analyzes original SL/TP levels.

âš ï¸ Conflict Details
  • Mid-Trade AI: Analyzes static original levels
  • Trailing/Breakeven: Changes those levels dynamically
  • Result: EA can interpret erroneous data â†’ inconsistent decisions
ğŸš« Incompatible Combination: Disable Mid-Trade if using Trailing or Breakeven systems.

âŒ Hidden SL/TP + Trailing/Breakeven

ğŸ”§ The Problem

Hidden SL/TP managed internally, but Trailing/Breakeven need to move them on broker.

âš ï¸ Conflict Details
  • Hidden SL/TP: Levels managed internally by EA
  • Trailing/Breakeven: Need to move levels on broker server
  • Result: Risk of desynchronization or closure failures
ğŸš« Critical Incompatibility: Use Hidden SL/TP only with static level management.

ğŸ”¶ Moderate Problems

âš ï¸ Overly Strict Filters + Very Low AI Confidence

ğŸ“Š Example Configuration
  • Minimum confidence: 50%
  • Fractals: 4 timeframes
  • News filter: Enabled
  • Result: Almost no trades executed
ğŸ’¡ Solution: Balance filters - if using multiple strict filters, increase AI confidence threshold or reduce filter quantity.

âš ï¸ Overlapping Timeframes in Fractals

ğŸ”§ The Problem

Including the trading timeframe within fractal confirmations.

ğŸ“Š Example
  • Trading on: M15
  • Fractal includes: M15, H1, H4
  • Result: Double redundant confirmation and unnecessary blocks
ğŸ’¡ Solution: Use fractal timeframes higher than your trading timeframe.

âš ï¸ Additional Timeframe + Fractals Misconfigured

ğŸ”§ The Problem

Both requesting validation on the same timeframe.

âš ï¸ Impact
  • Overweight confirmations: Too much validation on same timeframe
  • Frequency drop: Significant reduction in trade opportunities
  • Result: Over-filtering leads to missed trades
ğŸ’¡ Solution: Use different timeframes for Additional TF and Fractal confirmations.

âš ï¸ News Filter + Spread Filter + Volatility Thresholds Together

ğŸ”§ The Problem

In high volatility markets (e.g., GOLD), it's normal for all to coincide.

ğŸ“Š What Happens
  • News events: Block trading
  • High spreads: Block trading
  • High volatility: Block trading
  • Result: EA spends long periods without operating because all filters block simultaneously
ğŸ’¡ Solution: For volatile assets like GOLD, use maximum 2 of these 3 filters.

âš ï¸ Minor Compatibility Problems

ğŸ”¸ Hidden SL/TP + Unstable Connection (No VPS)

ğŸ”§ The Problem

If platform crashes, there are no stops on broker.

âš ï¸ Risk
  • Connection loss: Hidden levels become inactive
  • No broker protection: Only safety SL remains
  • Result: Risk of unlimited losses
ğŸš« Not Recommended: Hidden SL/TP without VPS or very stable connection.

ğŸ”¸ Support/Resistance + Very Tight ATR

ğŸ”§ The Problem

Can place stops too close to key levels.

ğŸ“Š Impact
  • Premature closures: Even when direction is correct
  • Tight stops: Near support/resistance levels
  • Result: Good trades closed too early
ğŸ’¡ Solution: Use wider ATR settings when S/R filter is active.

ğŸ”¸ Bullish Engulfing H4 + Multiple Fractals

ğŸ”§ The Problem

Both filters request trend confirmation on higher timeframes.

ğŸ“Š Impact
  • Double filtering: Both look for bullish confirmation
  • Reduced opportunities: Drastically fewer BUY trades
  • Over-confirmation: Too many requirements for same direction
ğŸ’¡ Solution: Use either Bullish Engulfing OR Fractal confirmations for BUY trades, not both.

ğŸ”¸ Volume Filter + News Filter

ğŸ”§ The Problem

During news, volume usually spikes.

âš ï¸ Contradiction
  • Volume filter: May allow trade due to high volume
  • News filter: Blocks trade due to news event
  • Result: Conflicting signals and missed opportunities
ğŸ’¡ Solution: Configure volume filter to also block during news events, or disable one of them.

ğŸ’¡ Additional Incompatibilities

ğŸ”¸ High Frequency Parameters + Multiple AI Consultation

ğŸ”§ The Problem

Very frequent AI queries with multiple AIs increase costs and latency.

ğŸ“Š Impact
  • High costs: Multiple AIs queried frequently
  • Slower responses: Multiple API calls per decision
  • API limits: Risk of hitting rate limits
ğŸ’¡ Solution: Use single AI for high-frequency trading, or reduce query frequency with multiple AIs.

ğŸ”¸ XGBoost ML + Very Low Confidence Threshold

ğŸ”§ The Problem

XGBoost provides high-confidence predictions, but low threshold accepts weak signals.

ğŸ“Š Impact
  • Contradictory logic: Advanced ML with weak signal acceptance
  • Noise trading: May execute on poor-quality signals
  • Reduced effectiveness: XGBoost advantage diminished
ğŸ’¡ Solution: When using XGBoost, maintain confidence threshold at 70%+ to leverage ML accuracy.

âœ… Best Practices to Avoid Conflicts

ğŸ¯ Configuration Guidelines

ğŸ“‹ Checklist Before Going Live:
  1. Choose ONE position management system: Trailing OR Breakeven OR Static
  2. If using Hidden SL/TP: Disable Mid-Trade, Trailing, and Breakeven
  3. Limit filter combinations: Maximum 3-4 active filters simultaneously
  4. Balance AI confidence with filters: More filters = higher confidence needed
  5. Test combinations on demo: Always verify compatibility before live trading
  6. Monitor performance: Watch for unexpected behavior or lack of trades
ğŸ”§ Remember: ARIA V4 is highly configurable, but with great power comes great responsibility. Understanding these incompatibilities will help you create robust, profitable configurations.

    Temperatura

    Temperatura de IA

    ğŸ“Œ CÃ³mo Funciona

    ğŸ§Š Temperatura Baja (ej. 0.0 â€“ 0.3)

    ğŸ¤– ConfiguraciÃ³n de IA Ãšnica

    ğŸ§  QuÃ© es XGBoost y CÃ³mo Maneja los Niveles SL/TP en ARIA

    ğŸ“ Proceso de Aprendizaje:

    ğŸ“° Filtro de Noticias

    ğŸ†• Indicador Visual V4: Cuando hay eventos de noticias activos para un par de divisas y ARIA no estÃ¡ operando debido a este filtro, el marco del grÃ¡fico aparecerÃ¡ en color rojo.     ğŸ“ ParÃ¡metros Fractales

    â“ Â¿QuÃ© es y para quÃ© sirve?

    Es un filtro de confirmaciÃ³n por confluencia de marcos temporales.     ğŸ”‘ Idea Clave: Confluencia = calidad. Sin confluencia o con seÃ±ales opuestas entre marcos temporales, el filtro niega la entrada.

    ğŸ† Reglas de Oro (Muy Importante)

    âš ï¸ Regla #1: Nunca incluyas el marco temporal de trading dentro del filtro fractal.
    • Ejemplo: Si operas en M5, activa M15 y superior (M15/M30/H1); no actives M5.
    • RazÃ³n: Evitar "auto-confirmaciÃ³n" y sobreajuste de la seÃ±al. Siempre confirma con marcos temporales superiores.
    • MÃ¡s marcos temporales = menos trades (filtro mÃ¡s estricto)
    • MÃ¡s confirmaciones mÃ­nimas = mÃ¡s selectivo (descarta mÃ¡s seÃ±ales)
    • Recomendado: Activar 2 confirmaciones de TFs superiores, ya que mÃ¡s perderÃ¡ muchas oportunidades de trading
    • Ajustar filtro al instrumento y su volatilidad (EURUSD â‰  GOLD)

    âš™ï¸ ParÃ¡metros (QuÃ© significan y cÃ³mo afectan)

    Habilitar Filtro Fractal

    Enciende/apaga el sistema de confluencia multi-TF.

    Marcos Temporales a Evaluar

    Selecciona los marcos temporales (ej. M15, M30, H1, H4, D1).

    Recuerda: Solo superiores al marco temporal donde operas y no mÃ¡s de 2 TF.
    Confirmaciones MÃ­nimas

    CuÃ¡ntos de los TFs seleccionados deben estar de acuerdo en la misma direcciÃ³n para permitir entrada.

    • 1â€“2 = mÃ¡s operaciones (mÃ¡s flexible)
    • 3â€“4 = menos operaciones (mÃ¡s exigente)
    PerÃ­odos de Lookback

    CuÃ¡ntas velas hacia atrÃ¡s mira cada TF para evaluar fractales/tendencia.

    • MÃ¡s lookback: SeÃ±ales mÃ¡s robustas, pero mÃ¡s tardÃ­as
    • Menos lookback: SeÃ±ales mÃ¡s rÃ¡pidas, pero mÃ¡s ruido
    Fuerza de Tendencia (Umbral)

    MÃ­nima "consistencia" (ej., 0.6) que el filtro debe detectar para aceptar.

    • Valor mÃ¡s alto: Reduce entradas en mercados laterales

    ğŸš¨ Problemas CrÃ­ticos

    âŒ Trailing Stop + Breakeven

    ğŸ”§ El Problema

    âš ï¸ Detalles del Conflicto

    ğŸš« Nunca Usar Juntos: Elige Trailing Stop O Breakeven, nunca ambos simultÃ¡neamente.

    âŒ Consultas Mid-Trade + Trailing/Breakeven

    • Resultado: EA puede interpretar datos errÃ³neos â†’ decisiones inconsistentes
    ğŸš« CombinaciÃ³n Incompatible: Deshabilitar Mid-Trade si usas sistemas Trailing o Breakeven.

    âŒ SL/TP Oculto + Trailing/Breakeven

    ğŸ”§ El Problema

    ğŸš« Incompatibilidad CrÃ­tica: Usar SL/TP Oculto solo con gestiÃ³n de niveles estÃ¡ticos.

    ğŸ”¶ Problemas Moderados

    âš ï¸ Filtros Excesivamente Estrictos + Confianza de IA Muy Baja

    âš ï¸ Marcos Temporales Superpuestos en Fractales

    ğŸ”§ El Problema

    âš ï¸ Marco Temporal Adicional + Fractales Mal Configurados

    âš ï¸ Filtro de Noticias + Filtro de Spread + Umbrales de Volatilidad Juntos
